فالصفة الدينية هي أن العقيدة الإسلامية توجب على المؤمنين احترام جميع الأحكام الفقهية التطبيقية التي تُفرّع على تلك المبادىء فيؤدوا الحقوق التي توجبها ولو كانوا بعيدين عن متناول القضاء لأنَّ إقامة العدل والمصالح من أمر الله بقول القرآن: ﴿إِنَّ اللَّهَ يَأْمُرُ بِالْعَدْلِ وَالْإِحْسَنِ ﴾ (سورة النحل : ٩٠/١٦ . ويشمل هذا الاحترام الأنظمة الزمنية الموقوتة المتبدلة التي يعود لولي الأمر القائم بالسلطة العليا حق إصدارها شرعاً بمقتضى قاعدة المصالح المرسلة التي سبقت الإشارة إليها. حتى إن فقهاءنا في المذهب الحنفي صرَّحوا بأنه إذا دعت الحاجة العامة والظروف الطارئة من اقتصادية أو غيرها إلى أن يأمر السلطان الناس بصيام يوم مثلاً فأمرهم وجب عليهم الصيام ديانة كصيام رمضان ما دام ذلك تنظيماً لمصلحة فوضه الشرع بتنظيمها. فالصفة الدينية في الفقه الإسلامي لا تنافي أنه مؤسس على قواعد مدنية بحتة منتجة لفقه متطوّر كفيل بوفاء الحاجات العصرية وحل المشكلات النابتة في الطريق، بل هذه الصفة الدينية دعامة وضمانة لاحترام المؤمنين الأحكام التشريعية كي لا يستبيحوا ما ليس لهم من حقوق الأفراد أو حقوق الدولة متى فقدت وسائل الإثبات أو كانوا في مأمن من طائلة القضاء كما تقدم بيانه فالصفة الدينية في الفقه الإسلامي مزيَّة فيه لا عيب والاحترام الناشيء عنها للأحكام التشريعية تتمناه اليوم القوانين الوضعية المحضة فلا تجده لأنفسها لأنه لا يأتي إلا من طريق العقيدة.
Chapter Twenty-One: Contemporary problems facing the application of Islamic Sharia today. 1/21 - Indeed, a group of the Islamic youth who grew up in a cultural environment that does not allow them to know the realities and vast capabilities of the legal system of Sharia see the impossibility of applying Islamic Sharia in the present age, because there are temporal problems that obstruct this application and Sharia is not sufficient to solve them in their view. We will present here brief points about these problems and the answer to them. 2/21 - The first problem: The religious character of Islamic Sharia. A group of foreign jurists delude, and this delusion has transferred to many Muslims, that Islamic Sharia is fixed religious rulings, so it does not accept the development required in modern laws according to temporal and economic conditions. The source of this delusion is ignorance of the meaning of religious character in the legal system of Sharia. Indeed, the civil part thereof, as is evident from the summary of principles we presented, includes its original legal texts in the Quran and prophetic hadith, legal principles and bases with fixed universal values, such as the principle of consent and good faith in contracts, and the principle of liability for harm and its compensation, etc., which modern positive laws have adopted today. The religious character is that the Islamic creed obligates the believers to respect all applied juristic rulings that are derived from those principles, so they fulfill the rights that are required even if they are far from the reach of the judiciary, because establishing justice and interests is from the command of Allah by the Quran: "Indeed, Allah commands justice and excellence" (Surah al-Nahl 16:90). This respect includes temporary time-bound changing regulations that the ruler possessing supreme authority has the right to issue legally according to the principle of Maslaha Mursala (unrestricted public interest) previously referenced. Even our jurists in the Hanafi school explicitly stated that if public need and urgent circumstances, whether economic or otherwise, require the ruler to order the people to fast a day, for example, and he orders them, then it becomes obligatory upon them to fast diyanatan (religiously) like the fast of Ramadan, as long as it is an organization for a benefit that the Law has entrusted him to organize. Thus, the religious character in Islamic fiqh does not contradict that it is founded on purely civil rules that produce a developed fiqh capable of fulfilling contemporary needs and solving problems that arise along the way. Rather, this religious character is a support and guarantee for the believers' respect for legislative rulings, so that they do not allow themselves what is not their right of individuals' rights or state rights when means of proof are lost or they are safe from the reach of the judiciary, as previously explained. So the religious character in Islamic fiqh is a merit, not a defect, and the respect arising from it for legislative rulings is desired today by purely positive laws, but they cannot find it for themselves because it only comes through creed.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage addresses the first contemporary problem: the misconception that Sharia's religious character makes it static and incapable of evolution. The author refutes this by clarifying that the religious character is a source of ethical obligation, not rigidity. He distinguishes between foundational universal principles—such as consent, good faith in contracts, and liability for harm—which are fixed, and the applied rulings derived from them, which can adapt to changing circumstances. The religious character ensures that believers comply with the law even in the absence of judicial enforcement, citing Quran 16:90. The author then emphasizes that temporary regulations fall under the ruler's authority based on the principle of maslaha mursala (unrestricted public interest). He gives a Hanafi example: if the ruler orders a communal fast due to urgent need, obedience is obligatory as a religious duty, analogized to fasting Ramadan. He concludes that the religious character is a strength—it guarantees respect for law from within—unlike purely positive laws that lack such moral foundation and thus cannot achieve the same level of voluntary compliance.

Key Terms
الصفة الدينية (al-sifatu al-diniyyah): The religious character that makes compliance with law a moral and creedal duty.
قاعدة المصالح المرسلة (qa'idatu al-masalih al-mursala): The principle of unrestricted public interest as a basis for legislation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Rigidity of rulings
B) Respect for legislative rulings even without judicial enforcement
C) That the ruler cannot issue temporary regulations
D) That Islamic law cannot adopt modern principles

Key Takeaway
The religious character is a strength that ensures ethical compliance without impeding legal evolution; the ruler can use maslaha mursala to regulate temporary needs.

The Principle of Averting Hudud by Doubts (Shubuhat)
Clarifying that hudud are rarely enforced due to strict conditions and the principle of shubuhat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of shubha to determine when a hadd punishment is dropped and replaced by ta'zir, and identify the underlying hadith.

Core Idea
Hudud punishments are designed to be rarely applied; mere doubt (shubha) drops the hadd and triggers ta'zir.

The second contemporary problem raised against Sharia is the alleged impossibility of applying hudud punishments today. This lesson examines the Hanafi response: hudud are strictly conditioned, and the prophetic command to avert hudud by doubts ensures they are seldom enforced. Instead, discretionary punishments (ta'zir) are applied when doubt exists. We will also introduce the principle of necessities (darurat) which further limits hudud in extraordinary circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
What is the contemporary objection regarding hudud mentioned in the text?
The objection claims hudud are impossible to apply in modern times.
2
State the Hanafi response
The passage gives two mechanisms: (1) strict conditions and shubha, (2) the maxim of necessities. Focus on the first.
3
Analyze the first mechanism: shubha
Explain the shubha principle: even a weak doubt drops the hadd and replaces it with ta'zir, based on the hadith.
The hadith is 'Avert the hudud by doubts'.
4
Understand the replacement: ta'zir
When hadd is dropped due to shubha, the judge imposes a discretionary punishment (ta'zir). Describe its nature.
Ta'zir ranges from reprimand to imprisonment.
5
Anticipate the second mechanism: darurat
The text mentions 'the principle of necessities' (qa'idat al-darurat) as another vast chapter. Think about how it further limits hudud in extraordinary circumstances.
This part is cut off; we will explore it in a future lesson.

3/21 - The second problem: Application of Hudud. This problem is (in their view that some of the bodily prescribed punishments (hudud) such as the punishment of the adulterer by flogging or stoning and the punishment of the thief by cutting off the hand have become impossible to apply in this age and the circumstances that have newly arisen. And the answer to that: That the hudud in Sharia, especially the hadd of zina, are conditioned by very narrow conditions in their proof and application, making them rarely applied. So they are dropped or changed to a discretionary punishment (ta'zir) determined by the judge merely by the existence of a doubt (shubha) on the part of the criminal, due to the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Avert the hudud by doubts.' And on the other hand, there exists in Sharia a vast chapter, which is the principle of necessities...
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage addresses the second contemporary problem: the alleged impossibility of applying hudud punishments today. The author answers by pointing out that hudud are deliberately made difficult to apply through strict evidenciary conditions; especially the hadd of zina requires extremely narrow conditions for proof and execution, making them rare. Crucially, if any doubt (shubha) exists regarding the crime or the criminal, the hadd punishment is waived and replaced by a discretionary punishment (ta'zir) determined by the judge. This is based on the prophetic command: 'Avert the hudud by doubts.' The passage then begins to mention another mechanism: the maxim of necessities (qa'idat al-darurat), which would further limit the application of hudud in extraordinary circumstances. However, the text cuts off. This illustrates Sharia's built-in flexibility to avoid harsh punishments unless proof is absolutely certain.

Key Terms
الحدود (al-hudud): Fixed corporal punishments prescribed by Sharia for specific crimes (e.g., zina, theft).
التعزير (al-ta'zir): Discretionary punishment determined by the judge when hadd conditions are not met.
شبهة (shubha): Doubt that prevents the application of hadd punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses the principle of shubha to ensure hudud are rarely applied, replacing them with ta'zir when any doubt exists.
